# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CRD Validation to OpenAPI Schema Publishing Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a CustomResourceDefinition's validation schema is converted to an OpenAPI schema in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find Go source files implementing: the CRD validation spec, the structural schema extraction, the OpenAPI v3 schema conversion, and the API server spec endpoint publication.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer document at `/workspace/answer.json` that traces the complete CRD validation schema to OpenAPI v3 conversion chain in Kubernetes.

## Summary

I've identified and documented the entire pipeline:

1. **CRD Validation Spec** - Defined in `CustomResourceValidation` type
2. **Structural Schema Extraction** - `NewStructural()` converts OpenAPI JSONSchemaProps to internal Structural format
3. **OpenAPI Conversion** - `ToKubeOpenAPI()` converts Structural back to go-openapi spec.Schema format
4. **Spec Building** - `BuildOpenAPIV3()` creates complete OpenAPI v3 specifications
5. **Dynamic Publishing Controller** - The OpenAPI v3 controller watches CRDs and publishes specs dynamically
6. **API Server Endpoint Setup** - `PrepareRun()` and `InstallV3()` register the `/openapi/v3` endpoints
7. **HTTP Handler** - `OpenAPIService` serves specs at runtime with caching support

The answer includes 13 key files, 10 important symbols, and a 9-step execution chain showing exactly how data flows through the system. The detailed narrative explains each component and how they work together to enable dynamic OpenAPI v3 schema publication for custom resources.

This is a faithful, roundtrippable conversion that preserves all structural schema information.\\n\\n### 4. OpenAPI Spec Building\\nThe CRD controller builds complete OpenAPI v3 specifications:\\n\\n- **BuildOpenAPIV3()** and **BuildOpenAPIV2()** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/controller/openapi/builder/builder.go:198-215`) take a CRD and construct full OpenAPI specifications. API Server Endpoint Registration\\nThe API server registers the OpenAPI v3 endpoint during startup:\\n\\n- **PrepareRun()** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:447-456`) calls `routes.OpenAPI.InstallV3()` to register the handler.\\n\\n- **InstallV3()** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/routes/openapi.go:52-59`) creates an OpenAPIService and registers it to handle `/openapi/v3` requests, returning discovery documents listing all available group/version specs with their relative URLs and etags for caching.\\n\\n### 7. HTTP Handler and Endpoint Publishing\\nThe kube-openapi handler serves the specs:\\n\\n- **OpenAPIService** (`vendor/k8s.io/kube-openapi/pkg/handler3/handler.go:49-60`) maintains a registry of OpenAPI v3 specifications indexed by group version.\\n\\n- **RegisterOpenAPIV3VersionedService()** registers HTTP handlers that:\\n  1. Serve the root `/openapi/v3` discovery document listing all group/versions\\n  2. Serve `/openapi/v3/apis/{group}/{version}` with the full spec for each group/version\\n  3. Include etags for client-side caching of specs\\n  4. Support both JSON and Protocol Buffer formats\\n\\n### Summary of Key Files and Functions\\nThe complete chain flows through:\\n1. CRD validation spec definition (`CustomResourceValidation`)\\n2. Structural schema extraction (`NewStructural()`)\\n3. OpenAPI conversion (`ToKubeOpenAPI()`)\\n4. Spec building (`BuildOpenAPIV3()`)\\n5. Dynamic controller updates (`Controller.buildV3Spec()`, `updateCRDSpec()`)\\n6. API server endpoint setup (`PrepareRun()`, `InstallV3()`)\\n7. HTTP handler serving (`OpenAPIService`, `RegisterOpenAPIV3VersionedService()`)\\n\\nThis architecture allows Kubernetes to dynamically publish OpenAPI v3 specifications for custom resources as they are defined via CustomResourceDefinitions, enabling clients to discover and validate custom resource schemas without restarting the API server.\"\n}\n",
